class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_1"><b><a href="#ref_1">^</a></b></span>  While <a href="/wiki/Sucre" title="Sucre">Sucre</a> is the constitutional capital, <a href="/wiki/La_Paz" title="La Paz">La Paz</a> is the seat of the government as member of the UCCI and the de facto capital. See <a href="/wiki/Bolivia#Capital" title="Bolivia">below</a>.</li>\n</ol></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>Bolivia</b> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="\'b\' in \'buy\'">b</span><span title="/&#601;/: \'a\' in \'about\'">&#601;</span><span title="/&#712;/: primary stress follows">&#712;</span><span title="\'l\' in \'lie\'">l</span><span title="/&#618;/: \'i\' in \'kit\'">&#618;</span><span title="\'v\' in \'vie\'">v</span><span title="/i/: \'y\' in \'happy\'">i</span><span title="/&#601;/: \'a\' in \'about\'">&#601;</span></span>/</a></span> <span class="nowrap" style="font-size:85%">(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap;margin-right:.25em;"><a href="/wiki/File:En-us-Bolivia.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" data-file-height="20" data-file-width="20" decoding="async" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" width="11"/></a></span><a class="internal" href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/3/39/En-us-Bolivia.ogg" title="En-us-Bolivia.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</span></span>, <small>Spanish:&#160;</small><span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Spanish" title="Help:IPA/Spanish">[bo&#712;li&#946;ja]</a></span>; <a href="/wiki/Guarani_language" title="Guarani language">Guarani</a>: <i lang="gn">Mborivia</i> <small></small><span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA" title="Help:IPA">[&#7504;bo&#712;&#638;i&#651;ja]</a></span>; <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Quechua_language" title="Quechua language">Quechua</a>: <i lang="qu">Puliwya</i> <small></small><span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Quechua" title="Help:IPA/Quechua">[p&#650;l&#618;wja]</a></span>; <a href="/wiki/Aymara_language" title="Aymara language">Aymara</a>: <i lang="ay">Wuliwya</i> <small></small><span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA" title="Help:IPA">[w&#650;l&#618;wja]</a></span>), officially the <b>Plurinational State of Bolivia</b> (<a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">Spanish</a>: <i lang="es">Estado Plurinacional de Bolivia</i> <small></small><span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Spanish" title="Help:IPA/Spanish">[es&#712;ta&#240;o plu&#638;inasjo&#712;nal de &#946;o&#712;li&#946;ja]</a></span>)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-8">[8]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> is a landlocked country located in western-central <a href="/wiki/South_America" title="South America">South America</a>. The capital is <a href="/wiki/Sucre" title="Sucre">Sucre</a> while the <a href="/wiki/Seat_of_government" title="Seat of government">seat of government</a> and financial center is located in <a href="/wiki/La_Paz" title="La Paz">La Paz</a>. The largest city and principal industrial center is <a href="/wiki/Santa_Cruz_de_la_Sierra" title="Santa Cruz de la Sierra">Santa Cruz de la Sierra</a>, located on the <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Bolivia" title="Geography of Bolivia">Llanos Orientales</a> (tropical lowlands) a mostly flat region in the east of Bolivia.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Sovereign_state" title="Sovereign state">sovereign state</a> of Bolivia is a <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Bolivia" title="Constitution of Bolivia">constitutionally</a> <a href="/wiki/Unitary_state" title="Unitary state">unitary state</a>, divided into <a href="/wiki/Departments_of_Bolivia" title="Departments of Bolivia">nine departments</a>. Its geography varies from the peaks of the <a href="/wiki/Andes" title="Andes">Andes</a> in the West, to the Eastern Lowlands, situated within the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Amazon_Basin" title="Amazon Basin">Amazon Basin</a>. It is bordered to the north and east by <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a>, to the southeast by <a href="/wiki/Paraguay" title="Paraguay">Paraguay</a>, to the south by <a href="/wiki/Argentina" title="Argentina">Argentina</a>, to the southwest by <a href="/wiki/Chile" title="Chile">Chile</a>, and to the northwest by <a href="/wiki/Peru" title="Peru">Peru</a>. One-third of the country is within the <a href="/wiki/Andes" title="Andes">Andean</a> mountain range. With 1,098,581&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (424,164&#160;sq&#160;mi) of area, Bolivia is the fifth largest country in <a href="/wiki/South_America" title="South America">South America</a> and the 27th largest in the world.\n</p><p>The country\'s population, estimated at 11&#160;million, is <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Multiethnic" title="Multiethnic">multiethnic</a>, including <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Amerindians" title="Amerindians">Amerindians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mestizo" title="Mestizo">Mestizos</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Europeans" title="Europeans">Europeans</a>, <a href="/wiki/Asian_people" title="Asian people">Asians</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Africans" title="Africans">Africans</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Racial_segregation" title="Racial segregation">racial</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Social_segregation" title="Social segregation">social segregation</a> that arose from Spanish colonialism has continued to the modern era. <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">Spanish</a> is the official and predominant language, although 36 <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Bolivia" title="Languages of Bolivia">indigenous languages</a> also have official status, of which the most commonly spoken are <a href="/wiki/Guarani_dialects" title="Guarani dialects">Guarani</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aymara_language" title="Aymara language">Aymara</a> and <a href="/wiki/Quechuan_languages" title="Quechuan languages">Quechua languages</a>.\n</p><p>Before Spanish colonization, the Andean region of Bolivia was part of the <a href="/wiki/Inca_Empire" title="Inca Empire">Inca Empire</a>, while the northern and eastern lowlands were inhabited by independent tribes. Spanish <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Conquistadors" title="Conquistadors">conquistadors</a></i> arriving from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cuzco" title="Cuzco">Cuzco</a> and <a href="/wiki/Asunci%C3%B3n" title="Asunci&#243;n">Asunci&#243;n</a> took control of the region in the 16th century. During the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Empire" title="Spanish Empire">Spanish colonial period</a> Bolivia was administered by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Royal_Audiencia_of_Charcas" title="Royal Audiencia of Charcas">Royal Audiencia of Charcas</a>. Spain built its empire in large part upon the silver that was extracted from <a href="/wiki/Mining_in_Bolivia" title="Mining in Bolivia">Bolivia\'s mines</a>.\nAfter the first call for independence in 1809, 16 years of war followed before the establishment of the Republic, named for <a href="/wiki/Sim%C3%B3n_Bol%C3%ADvar" title="Sim&#243;n Bol&#237;var">Sim&#243;n Bol&#237;var</a>. Over the course of the 19th and early 20th century Bolivia lost control of several peripheral territories to neighboring countries including the <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Pacific" title="War of the Pacific">seizure</a> of its coastline by Chile in 1879. Bolivia remained relatively politically stable until 1971, when <a href="/wiki/Hugo_Banzer" title="Hugo Banzer">Hugo Banzer</a> led a <a href="/wiki/History_of_Bolivia_(1964%E2%80%9382)#The_Banzer_regime" title="History of Bolivia (1964&#8211;82)">coup d\'&#233;tat</a> which replaced the socialist government of <a href="/wiki/Juan_Jos%C3%A9_Torres" title="Juan Jos&#233; Torres">Juan Jos&#233; Torres</a> with a <a href="/wiki/Military_dictatorship" title="Military dictatorship">military dictatorship</a> headed by Banzer; Torres was murdered in <a href="/wiki/Buenos_Aires" title="Buenos Aires">Buenos Aires</a>, <a href="/wiki/Argentina" title="Argentina">Argentina</a> by a right-wing death squad in 1976. Banzer\'s regime cracked down on <a href="/wiki/Left-wing_politics" title="Left-wing politics">leftist and socialist</a> opposition and other forms of dissent, resulting in the torture and deaths of a number of Bolivian citizens. Banzer was ousted in 1978 and later returned as the democratically elected president of Bolivia from 1997 to 2001.\n</p><p>Modern Bolivia is a charter member of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">UN</a>, <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">IMF</a>, <a href="/wiki/Non-Aligned_Movement" title="Non-Aligned Movement">NAM</a>, <a href="/wiki/Organization_of_American_States" title="Organization of American States">OAS</a>, <a href="/wiki/Amazon_Cooperation_Treaty_Organization" title="Amazon Cooperation Treaty Organization">ACTO</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bank_of_the_South" title="Bank of the South">Bank of the South</a>, <a href="/wiki/ALBA" title="ALBA">ALBA</a> and <a href="/wiki/Union_of_South_American_Nations" title="Union of South American Nations">USAN</a>. For over a decade Bolivia has had<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (February 2019)">when?</span></a></i>]</sup> one of the highest economic growth rates in Latin America; however, it remains the second poorest country in South America.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IMFUNASURGDP_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-IMFUNASURGDP-10">[10]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TELESUR_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-TELESUR-11">[11]</a></sup> It is a <a href="/wiki/Developing_country" title="Developing country">developing country</a>, with a medium ranking in the <a href="/wiki/Human_Development_Index" title="Human Development Index">Human Development Index</a>, a poverty level of 38.6%,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> and one of the lowest crime rates in <a href="/wiki/Latin_America" title="Latin America">Latin America</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> Its main economic activities include <a href="/wiki/Agriculture" title="Agriculture">agriculture</a>, <a href="/wiki/Forestry" title="Forestry">forestry</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fishing" title="Fishing">fishing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mining" title="Mining">mining</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Manufacturing" title="Manufacturing">manufacturing</a> goods such as textiles, clothing, refined metals, and <a href="/wiki/Oil_refinery" title="Oil refinery">refined petroleum</a>. Bolivia is very <a href="/wiki/Geology_of_Bolivia" title="Geology of Bolivia">rich in minerals</a>, including <a href="/wiki/Tin" title="Tin">tin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Silver" title="Silver">silver</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Lithium" title="Lithium">lithium</a>.\n</p>\n<div class="toc" id="toc"><input class="toctogglecheckbox" id="toctogglecheckbox" role="button" style="display:none" type="checkbox"/><div class="toctitle" dir="ltr" lang="en"><h2>Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" for="toctogglecheckbox"></label></span></div>\n<ul>\n<li wars</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-6"><a href="#Early_20th_century"><span class="tocnumber">2.4</span> <span class="toctext">Early 20th century</span></a></li>\n<li assets</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-11"><a href="#Geography"><span class="tocnumber">3</span> <span class="toctext">Geography</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li divisions</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-22"><a href="#Economy"><span class="tocnumber">6</span> <span class="toctext">Economy</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 class="toclevel-2 tocsection-28"><a href="#Water_supply_and_sanitation"><span class="tocnumber">7.4</span> <span class="toctext">Water supply and sanitation</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-29"><a href="#Demographics"><span class="tocnumber">8</span> <span class="toctext">Demographics</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-30"><a href="#Genetics"><span class="tocnumber">8.1</span> <span class="toctext">Genetics</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-31"><a href="#Ethnic_and_racial_classifications"><span class="tocnumber">8.2.1</span> <span class="toctext">Indigenous peoples</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-33"><a href="#Language"><span class="tocnumber">8.3</span> <span class="toctext">Language</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-34"><a href="#Religion"><span class="tocnumber">8.4</span> <span class="toctext">Religion</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-35"><a href="#Largest_cities_and_towns"><span class="tocnumber">8.5</span> <span class="toctext">Largest cities and towns</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-36"><a href="#Culture"><span class="tocnumber">9</span> <span class="toctext">Culture</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-37"><a href="#Education"><span class="tocnumber">10</span> <span class="toctext">Education</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-38"><a href="#Health"><span class="tocnumber">11</span> <span class="toctext">Health</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-39"><a href="#Sports"><span class="tocnumber">12</span> <span class="toctext">Sports</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-40"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">13</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-41"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">14</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-42"><a href="#Bibliography"><span class="tocnumber">15</span> <span class="toctext">Bibliography</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-43"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">16</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bolivia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Bolivia is named after Sim&#243;n Bol&#237;var, a leader in the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_American_wars_of_independence" title="Spanish American wars of independence">Spanish American wars of independence</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> The leader of <a href="/wiki/Venezuela" title="Venezuela">Venezuela</a>, <a href="/wiki/Antonio_Jos%C3%A9_de_Sucre" title="Antonio Jos&#233; de Sucre">Antonio Jos&#233; de Sucre</a>, had been given the option by Bol&#237;var to either unite <a href="/wiki/Sucre" title="Sucre">Charcas</a> (present-day Bolivia) with the newly formed <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Republic_of_Peru" title="Republic of Peru">Republic of Peru</a>, to unite with the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_Provinces_of_Rio_de_la_Plata" title="United Provinces of Rio de la Plata">United Provinces of Rio de la Plata</a>, or to formally declare its independence from Spain as a wholly independent state. Sucre opted to create a brand new state and on 6 August 1825, with local support, named it in honor of Sim&#243;n Bol&#237;var.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The original name was Republic of Bol&#237;var. Some days later, congressman Manuel Mart&#237;n Cruz proposed: "If from <a href="/wiki/Romulus" title="Romulus">Romulus</a> comes Rome, then from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bol%C3%ADvar" title="Bol&#237;var">Bol&#237;var</a> comes Bolivia" (Spanish: <i lang="es">Si de R&#243;mulo Roma, de Bol&#237;var Bolivia</i>). The name was approved by the Republic on 3 October 1825.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Blogs.law.harvard.edu_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-Blogs.law.harvard.edu-16">[16]</a></sup> In 2009, a <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Bolivia" title="Constitution of Bolivia">new constitution</a> changed the country\'s official name to "Plurinational State of Bolivia" in recognition of the multi-ethnic nature of the country and the enhanced position of Bolivia\'s indigenous peoples under the new constitution.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Blogs.law.harvard.edu_16-1"><a href="#cite_note-Blogs.law.harvard.edu-16">[16]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bolivia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Bolivia" title="History of Bolivia">History of Bolivia</a></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Pre-colonial">Pre-colonial</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bolivia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Pre-colonial">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Puerta_del_Sol_S%C3%ADmbolo_de_Tiwanaku_-_Bolivia.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1536" data-file-width="2048" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Puerta_del_Sol_S%C3%ADmbolo_de_Tiwanaku_-_Bolivia.jpg/220px-Puerta_del_Sol_S%C3%ADmbolo_de_Tiwanaku_-_Bolivia.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Puerta_del_Sol_S%C3%ADmbolo_de_Tiwanaku_-_Bolivia.jpg/330px-Puerta_del_Sol_S%C3%ADmbolo_de_Tiwanaku_-_Bolivia.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Puerta_del_Sol_S%C3%ADmbolo_de_Tiwanaku_-_Bolivia.jpg/440px-Puerta_del_Sol_S%C3%ADmbolo_de_Tiwanaku_-_Bolivia.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Puerta_del_Sol_S%C3%ADmbolo_de_Tiwanaku_-_Bolivia.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Gate_of_the_Sun" title="Gate of the Sun">Puerta del Sol</a>, Archaeological Zone of <a href="/wiki/Tiwanaku" title="Tiwanaku">Tiwanaku</a>, Bolivia</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Map_of_Wari_and_Tiawaku.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="365" data-file-width="267" decoding="async" height="301" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Map_of_Wari_and_Tiawaku.svg/220px-Map_of_Wari_and_Tiawaku.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Map_of_Wari_and_Tiawaku.svg/330px-Map_of_Wari_and_Tiawaku.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Map_of_Wari_and_Tiawaku.svg/440px-Map_of_Wari_and_Tiawaku.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Map_of_Wari_and_Tiawaku.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Tiwanaku at its largest territorial extent, AD 950</div></div></div>\n<p>The region now known as Bolivia had been occupied for over 2,500 years when the <a href="/wiki/Aymara_people" title="Aymara people">Aymara</a> arrived. However, present-day Aymara associate themselves with the ancient civilization of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tiwanaku_culture" title="Tiwanaku culture">Tiwanaku culture</a> which had its capital at <a href="/wiki/Tiwanaku" title="Tiwanaku">Tiwanaku</a>, in Western Bolivia. The capital city of Tiwanaku dates from as early as 1500 BC when it was a small, agriculturally based village.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The community grew to urban proportions between AD 600 and AD 800, becoming an important regional power in the southern <a href="/wiki/Andes" title="Andes">Andes</a>. According to early estimates,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (February 2014)">when?</span></a></i>]</sup> the city covered approximately 6.5 square kilometers (2.5 square miles) at its maximum extent and had between 15,000 and 30,000 inhabitants.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> In 1996 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Satellite_imaging" title="Satellite imaging">satellite imaging</a> was used to map the extent of fossilized suka kollus (flooded raised fields) across the three primary valleys of Tiwanaku, arriving at population-carrying capacity estimates of anywhere between 285,000 and 1,482,000 people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Valley_of_the_Spirits_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-Valley_of_the_Spirits-19">[19]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Around AD 400, Tiwanaku went from being a locally dominant force to a predatory state. Tiwanaku expanded its reaches into the Yungas and brought its culture and way of life to many other cultures in Peru, Bolivia, and Chile. Tiwanaku was not a violent culture in many respects. In order to expand its reach, Tiwanaku exercised great political astuteness, creating colonies, fostering trade agreements (which made the other cultures rather dependent), and instituting state cults.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-McAndrews,_Timothy_L._1997_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-McAndrews,_Timothy_L._1997-20">[20]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The empire continued to grow with no end in sight. William H. Isbell states "Tiahuanaco underwent a dramatic transformation between AD 600 and 700 that established new monumental standards for civic architecture and greatly increased the resident population."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> Tiwanaku continued to absorb cultures rather than eradicate them. Archaeologists note a dramatic adoption of Tiwanaku ceramics into the cultures which became part of the Tiwanaku empire. Tiwanaku\'s power was further solidified through the trade it implemented among the cities within its empire.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-McAndrews,_Timothy_L._1997_20-1"><a href="#cite_note-McAndrews,_Timothy_L._1997-20">[20]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Tiwanaku\'s elites gained their status through the surplus food they controlled, collected from outlying regions and then redistributed to the general populace. Further, this elite\'s control of <a href="/wiki/Llama" title="Llama">llama</a> herds became a powerful control mechanism as llamas were essential for carrying goods between the civic centre and the periphery. These herds also came to symbolize class distinctions between the commoners and the elites. Through this control and manipulation of surplus resources, the elite\'s power continued to grow until about AD 950. At this time a dramatic shift in climate occurred,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kolata,_Alan_L._1993_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-Kolata,_Alan_L._1993-22">[22]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (July 2013)">page&#160;needed</span></a></i>]</sup> causing a significant drop in precipitation in the Titicaca Basin, believed by archaeologists to have been on the scale of a major drought.\n</p><p>As the rainfall decreased, many of the cities farther away from Lake Titicaca began to tender fewer foodstuffs to the elites. As the surplus of food decreased, and thus the amount available to underpin their power, the control of the elites began to falter. The capital city became the last place viable for food production due to the resiliency of the raised field method of agriculture. Tiwanaku disappeared around AD 1000 because food production, the main source of the elites\' power, dried up. The area remained uninhabited for centuries thereafter.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kolata,_Alan_L._1993_22-1"><a href="#cite_note-Kolata,_Alan_L._1993-22">[22]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Inca_Expansion.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="926" data-file-width="512" decoding="async" height="398" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Inca_Expansion.svg/220px-Inca_Expansion.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Inca_Expansion.svg/330px-Inca_Expansion.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Inca_Expansion.svg/440px-Inca_Expansion.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Inca_Expansion.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Inca Expansion (1438&#8211;1533)</div></div></div>\n<p>Between 1438 and 1527, the Inca empire, during its expansion from its capital at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cuzco" title="Cuzco">Cuzco</a>, <a href="/wiki/Peru" title="Peru">Peru</a>. It gained control over much of what is now Andean Bolivia and extended its control into the fringes of the Amazon basin.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Colonial_period">Colonial period</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bolivia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Colonial period">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The Spanish conquest of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Inca_empire" title="Inca empire">Inca empire</a> began in 1524, and was mostly completed by 1533. The territory now called Bolivia was known as Charcas, and was under the authority of the Viceroy of <a href="/wiki/Lima" title="Lima">Lima</a>. Local government came from the <a href="/wiki/Real_Audiencia_of_Charcas" title="Real Audiencia of Charcas">Audiencia de Charcas</a> located in Chuquisaca (La Plata&#8212;modern <a href="/wiki/Sucre" title="Sucre">Sucre</a>). Founded in 1545 as a mining town, <a href="/wiki/Potos%C3%AD" title="Potos&#237;">Potos&#237;</a> soon produced fabulous wealth, becoming the largest city in the <a href="/wiki/New_World" title="New World">New World</a> with a population exceeding 150,000 people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup>\n</p><p>By the late 16th century, Bolivian <a href="/wiki/Silver" title="Silver">silver</a> was an important source of revenue for the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Empire" title="Spanish Empire">Spanish Empire</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> A steady stream of natives served as labor force under the brutal, slave conditions of the Spanish version of the pre-Columbian draft system called the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mita_(Inca)" title="Mita (Inca)">mita</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> Charcas was transferred to the <a href="/wiki/Viceroyalty_of_the_R%C3%ADo_de_la_Plata" title="Viceroyalty of the R&#237;o de la Plata">Viceroyalty of the R&#237;o de la Plata</a> in 1776 and the people from Buenos Aires, the capital of the Viceroyalty, coined the term "<a href="/wiki/Upper_Peru" title="Upper Peru">Upper Peru</a>" (<a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">Spanish</a>: <i lang="es">Alto Per&#250;</i>) as a popular reference to the Royal Audiencia of Charcas. <a href="/wiki/T%C3%BApac_Katari" title="T&#250;pac Katari">T&#250;pac Katari</a> led the indigenous rebellion that laid siege to <a href="/wiki/La_Paz" title="La Paz">La Paz</a> in March 1781,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> during which 20,000 people died.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> As Spanish royal authority weakened during the <a href="/wiki/Napoleonic_Wars" title="Napoleonic Wars">Napoleonic wars</a>, sentiment against colonial rule grew.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Independence_and_subsequent_wars">Independence and subsequent wars</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bolivia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Independence and subsequent wars">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Bolivia_(1809%E2%80%931920)" title="History of Bolivia (1809&#8211;1920)">History of Bolivia (1809&#8211;1920)</a></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Bolivian_War_of_Independence" title="Bolivian War of Independence">struggle for independence</a> started in the city of <a href="/wiki/Sucre" title="Sucre">Sucre</a> on 25 May 1809 and the <a href="/wiki/Chuquisaca_Revolution" title="Chuquisaca Revolution">Chuquisaca Revolution</a> (Chuquisaca was then the name of the city) is known as the first cry of Freedom in Latin America. That revolution was followed by the <a href="/wiki/La_Paz_revolution" title="La Paz revolution">La Paz revolution</a> on 16 July 1809. The La Paz revolution marked a complete split with the Spanish government, while the Chuquisaca Revolution established a local independent junta in the name of the Spanish King deposed by Napoleon Bonaparte. Both revolutions were short-lived and defeated by the Spanish authorities in the Viceroyalty of the Rio de La Plata, but the following year the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_American_wars_of_independence" title="Spanish American wars of independence">Spanish American wars of independence</a> raged across the continent.\n</p><p>Bolivia was captured and recaptured many times during the war by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Royalist_(Spanish_American_Revolution)" title="Royalist (Spanish American Revolution)">royalists</a> and patriots. Buenos Aires sent three military campaigns, all of which were defeated, and eventually limited itself to protecting the national borders at Salta. Bolivia was finally freed of Royalist dominion by <a href="/wiki/Antonio_Jos%C3%A9_de_Sucre" title="Antonio Jos&#233; de Sucre">Antonio Jos&#233; de Sucre</a>, with a military campaign coming from the North in support of the campaign of <a href="/wiki/Sim%C3%B3n_Bol%C3%ADvar" title="Sim&#243;n Bol&#237;var">Sim&#243;n Bol&#237;var</a>. After 16 years of war the Republic was <a href="/wiki/Bolivian_Declaration_of_Independence" title="Bolivian Declaration of Independence">proclaimed</a> on 6 August 1825.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Coat_of_arms_of_Bolivia_(1825).svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="597" data-file-width="478" decoding="async" height="275" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Coat_of_arms_of_Bolivia_%281825%29.svg/220px-Coat_of_arms_of_Bolivia_%281825%29.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Coat_of_arms_of_Bolivia_%281825%29.svg/330px-Coat_of_arms_of_Bolivia_%281825%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Coat_of_arms_of_Bolivia_%281825%29.svg/440px-Coat_of_arms_of_Bolivia_%281825%29.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Coat_of_arms_of_Bolivia_(1825).svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The first coat of arms of Bolivia, formerly named the Republic of Bol&#237;var in honor of <a href="/wiki/Sim%C3%B3n_Bol%C3%ADvar" title="Sim&#243;n Bol&#237;var">Sim&#243;n Bol&#237;var</a></div></div></div>\n<p>In 1836, Bolivia, under the rule of <a href="/wiki/Marshal" title="Marshal">Marshal</a> <a href="/wiki/Andr%C3%A9s_de_Santa_Cruz" title="Andr&#233;s de Santa Cruz">Andr&#233;s de Santa Cruz</a>, invaded Peru to reinstall the deposed president, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/General" title="General">General</a> <a href="/wiki/Luis_Jos%C3%A9_de_Orbegoso" title="Luis Jos&#233; de Orbegoso">Luis Jos&#233; de Orbegoso</a>. Peru and Bolivia formed the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Peru-Bolivian_Confederation" title="Peru-Bolivian Confederation">Peru-Bolivian Confederation</a>, with de Santa Cruz as the <i>Supreme Protector</i>. Following tension between the Confederation and Chile, Chile declared war on 28 December 1836. Argentina separately declared war on the Confederation on 9 May 1837. The Peruvian-Bolivian forces achieved several major victories during the <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Confederation" title="War of the Confederation">War of the Confederation</a>: the defeat of the Argentine expedition and the defeat of the first Chilean expedition on the fields of <a href="/wiki/Paucarpata_District" title="Paucarpata District">Paucarpata</a> near the city of <a href="/wiki/Arequipa" title="Arequipa">Arequipa</a>.\n</p><p>At the outset of the war, the Chilean and Peruvian rebel army surrendered unconditionally and signed the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Paucarpata_Treaty&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Paucarpata Treaty (page does not exist)">Paucarpata Treaty</a>. The treaty stipulated that Chile would withdraw from Peru-Bolivia, Chile would return captured Confederate ships, economic relations would be normalized, and the Confederation would pay Peruvian debt to Chile. In Chile, the government and public rejected the peace treaty. Chile organized a second attack on the Confederation and defeated it in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Yungay" title="Battle of Yungay">Battle of Yungay</a>. After this defeat, Santa Cruz resigned and went to exile in <a href="/wiki/Ecuador" title="Ecuador">Ecuador</a> and then Paris, and the Peruvian-Bolivian Confederation was dissolved.\n</p><p>Following the renewed independence of Peru, Peruvian president General <a href="/wiki/Agust%C3%ADn_Gamarra" title="Agust&#237;n Gamarra">Agust&#237;n Gamarra</a> invaded Bolivia. The Peruvian army was decisively defeated at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Ingavi" title="Battle of Ingavi">Battle of Ingavi</a> on 20 November 1841 where Gamarra was killed. The Bolivian army under General <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Ballivi%C3%A1n" title="Jos&#233; Ballivi&#225;n">Jos&#233; Ballivi&#225;n</a> then mounted a counter-offensive, capturing the Peruvian port of <a href="/wiki/Arica_Province_(Peru)" title="Arica Province (Peru)">Arica</a>. Later, both sides signed a <a href="/wiki/Peace_treaty" title="Peace treaty">peace treaty</a> in 1842, putting a final end to the war.\n</p><p>A period of political and economic instability in the early-to-mid-19th century weakened Bolivia. In addition, during the <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Pacific" title="War of the Pacific">War of the Pacific</a> (1879&#8211;83), <a href="/wiki/Chile" title="Chile">Chile</a> occupied vast territories rich in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Natural_resources" title="Natural resources">natural resources</a> south west of Bolivia, including the Bolivian <a href="/wiki/Coast" title="Coast">coast</a>. Chile took control of today\'s <a href="/wiki/Chuquicamata" title="Chuquicamata">Chuquicamata</a> area, the adjoining rich <i>salitre</i> (<a href="/wiki/Sodium_nitrate" title="Sodium nitrate">saltpeter</a>) fields, and the port of <a href="/wiki/Antofagasta" title="Antofagasta">Antofagasta</a> among other Bolivian territories.\n</p><p>Thus, since independence, Bolivia has lost over half of its territory to neighboring countries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> It also lost the <a href="/wiki/Acre_(state)" title="Acre (state)">state of Acre</a>, in the <a href="/wiki/Acre_War" title="Acre War">Acre War</a>, important because this region was known for its production of rubber. Peasants and the Bolivian army fought briefly but after a few victories, and facing the prospect of a total war against Brazil, it was forced to sign the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Petr%C3%B3polis" title="Treaty of Petr&#243;polis">Treaty of Petr&#243;polis</a> in 1903, in which Bolivia lost this rich territory. Popular myth has it that Bolivian president Mariano Melgarejo (1864&#8211;71) traded the land for what he called "a magnificent white horse" and Acre was subsequently flooded by Brazilians, which ultimately led to confrontation and fear of war with Brazil.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> In the late 19th century, an increase in the world price of silver brought Bolivia relative prosperity and political stability.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_20th_century">Early 20th century</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bolivia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Early 20th century">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Bolivia_(1920%E2%80%9364)" title="History of Bolivia (1920&#8211;64)">History of Bolivia (1920&#8211;64)</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Map_Bolivia_territorial_loss-en.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="355" data-file-width="375" decoding="async" height="208" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Map_Bolivia_territorial_loss-en.svg/220px-Map_Bolivia_territorial_loss-en.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Map_Bolivia_territorial_loss-en.svg/330px-Map_Bolivia_territorial_loss-en.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Map_Bolivia_territorial_loss-en.svg/440px-Map_Bolivia_territorial_loss-en.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Map_Bolivia_territorial_loss-en.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Bolivia\'s territorial losses (1867&#8211;1938)</div></div></div>\n<p>During the early 20th century, <a href="/wiki/Tin" title="Tin">tin</a> replaced silver as the country\'s most important source of wealth. A succession of governments controlled by the economic and social elite followed <a href="/wiki/Laissez-faire" title="Laissez-faire">laissez-faire</a> capitalist policies through the first 30 years of the 20th century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Living conditions of the native people, who constitute most of the population, remained deplorable. With work opportunities limited to primitive conditions in the mines and in large estates having nearly feudal status, they had no access to education, economic opportunity, and <a href="/wiki/Participation_(decision_making)" title="Participation (decision making)">political participation</a>. Bolivia\'s defeat by Paraguay in the <a href="/wiki/Chaco_War" title="Chaco War">Chaco War</a> (1932&#8211;35), where Bolivia lost a great part of the <a href="/wiki/Gran_Chaco" title="Gran Chaco">Gran Chaco</a> region in dispute, marked a turning-point.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Revolutionary_Nationalist_Movement" title="Revolutionary Nationalist Movement">Revolutionary Nationalist Movement</a> (MNR), the most historic political party, emerged as a broad-based party. Denied its victory in the 1951 presidential elections, the MNR led a successful revolution in 1952. Under President <a href="/wiki/V%C3%ADctor_Paz_Estenssoro" title="V&#237;ctor Paz Estenssoro">V&#237;ctor Paz Estenssoro</a>, the MNR, having strong popular pressure, introduced <a href="/wiki/Universal_suffrage" title="Universal suffrage">universal suffrage</a> into his political platform and carried out a sweeping land-reform promoting rural education and nationalization of the country\'s largest tin mines.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Late_20th_century">Late 20th century</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bolivia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Late 20th century">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Bolivia_(1964%E2%80%9382)" title="History of Bolivia (1964&#8211;82)">History of Bolivia (1964&#8211;82)</a></div>\n<p>Twelve years of tumultuous rule left the MNR divided. In 1964, a military <a href="/wiki/Military_dictatorship" title="Military dictatorship">junta</a> overthrew President Estenssoro at the outset of his third term. The 1969 death of President <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ren%C3%A9_Barrientos_Ortu%C3%B1o" title="Ren&#233; Barrientos Ortu&#241;o">Ren&#233; Barrientos Ortu&#241;o</a>, a former member of the junta who was elected president in 1966, led to a succession of weak governments. Alarmed by the rising Popular Assembly and the increase in the popularity of President Juan Jos&#233; Torres, the military, the MNR, and others installed Colonel (later General) <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hugo_Banzer_Su%C3%A1rez" title="Hugo Banzer Su&#225;rez">Hugo Banzer Su&#225;rez</a> as president in 1971. He returned to the presidency in 1997 through 2001.\n</p><p>The United States\' <a href="/wiki/Central_Intelligence_Agency" title="Central Intelligence Agency">Central Intelligence Agency</a> (CIA) had been active in providing finances and training to the Bolivian military dictatorship in the 1960s. The revolutionary leader <a href="/wiki/Che_Guevara" title="Che Guevara">Che Guevara</a> was killed by a team of CIA officers and members of the Bolivian Army on 9 October 1967, in Bolivia. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/F%C3%A9lix_Rodr%C3%ADguez_(Central_Intelligence_Agency)" title="F&#233;lix Rodr&#237;guez (Central Intelligence Agency)">F&#233;lix Rodr&#237;guez</a> was a CIA officer on the team with the Bolivian Army that captured and shot Guevara.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC-2007-10-8_33-0"><a href="#cite_note-BBC-2007-10-8-33">[33]</a></sup> Rodriguez said that after he received a Bolivian presidential execution order, he told "the soldier who pulled the trigger to aim carefully, to remain consistent with the Bolivian government\'s story that Che had been killed in action during a clash with the Bolivian army." Rodriguez said the US government had wanted Che in Panama, and "I could have tried to falsify the command to the troops, and got Che to Panama as the US government said they had wanted", but that he had chosen to "let history run its course" as desired by Bolivia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-XXXI-172_34-0"><a href="#cite_note-XXXI-172-34">[34]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Elections in 1979 and 1981 were inconclusive and marked by fraud. There were coups d\'&#233;tat, counter-coups, and caretaker governments. In 1980, General <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Luis_Garc%C3%ADa_Meza_Tejada" title="Luis Garc&#237;a Meza Tejada">Luis Garc&#237;a Meza Tejada</a> carried out a ruthless and violent <a href="/wiki/Coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="Coup d\'&#233;tat">coup d\'&#233;tat</a> that did not have popular support. He pacified the people by promising to remain in power only for one year. At the end of the year, he staged a televised rally to claim popular support and announced, "<i>Bueno, me quedo</i>", or, "All right; I\'ll stay [in office]."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> After a military rebellion forced out Meza in 1981, three other military governments in 14 months struggled with Bolivia\'s growing problems. Unrest forced the military to convoke the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_Congress_of_Bolivia" title="National Congress of Bolivia">Congress</a>, elected in 1980, and allow it to choose a new chief executive. In October 1982, <a href="/wiki/Hern%C3%A1n_Siles_Zuazo" title="Hern&#225;n Siles Zuazo">Hern&#225;n Siles Zuazo</a> again became president, 22 years after the end of his first term of office (1956&#8211;60).\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Democratic_transition">Democratic transition</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bolivia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Democratic transition">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Bolivia_(1982%E2%80%93present)" title="History of Bolivia (1982&#8211;present)">History of Bolivia (1982&#8211;present)</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Gonzalo_sanchez_de_lozada.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="266" data-file-width="200" decoding="async" height="266" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/0/04/Gonzalo_sanchez_de_lozada.jpg" width="200"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Gonzalo_sanchez_de_lozada.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Former President, <a href="/wiki/Gonzalo_S%C3%A1nchez_de_Lozada" title="Gonzalo S&#225;nchez de Lozada">Gonzalo S&#225;nchez de Lozada</a></div></div></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Gonzalo_S%C3%A1nchez_de_Lozada" title="Gonzalo S&#225;nchez de Lozada">Gonzalo S&#225;nchez de Lozada</a> pursued an aggressive economic and social reform agenda. The most dramatic reform was privatization under the "capitalization" program, under which investors, typically foreign, acquired 50% ownership and management control of public enterprises in return for agreed upon capital investments.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1993, <a href="/wiki/Gonzalo_S%C3%A1nchez_de_Lozada" title="Gonzalo S&#225;nchez de Lozada">Gonzalo S&#225;nchez de Lozada</a> ran for <a href="/wiki/President_of_Bolivia" title="President of Bolivia">president</a> in alliance with the <a href="/wiki/Revolutionary_Liberation_Movement_Tupaq_Katari" title="Revolutionary Liberation Movement Tupaq Katari">Tupac Katari Revolutionary Liberation Movement</a>, which inspired indigenous-sensitive and multicultural-aware policies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> In 1993, Sanchez de Lozada introduced the <i>Plan de Todos</i>, which led to the decentralization of government, introduction of <a href="/wiki/Intercultural_bilingual_education" title="Intercultural bilingual education">intercultural bilingual education</a>, implementation of <a href="/wiki/Agriculture" title="Agriculture">agrarian</a> <a href="/wiki/Legislation" title="Legislation">legislation</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Privatization" title="Privatization">privatization</a> of state owned businesses. The plan explicitly stated that Bolivian citizens would own a minimum of 51% of enterprises; under the plan, most <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Government-owned_corporation" title="Government-owned corporation">state-owned enterprises</a> (SOEs), though not mines, were sold.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> This privatization of SOEs led to a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Neoliberal" title="Neoliberal">neoliberal</a> structuring.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Law of Popular Participation dumped upon municipalities the responsibility of maintaining various infrastructures (and offering services): health, education, systems of irrigation, without support from the state.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (October 2014)">when?</span></a></i>]</sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The reforms and economic restructuring were strongly opposed by certain segments of society, which instigated frequent and sometimes violent protests, particularly in La Paz and the Chapare <a href="/wiki/Coca" title="Coca">coca</a>-growing region, from 1994 through 1996. The indigenous population of the <a href="/wiki/Andes" title="Andes">Andean</a> region was not able to benefit from government reforms.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> During this time, the umbrella labor-organization of Bolivia, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Central_Obrera_Boliviana" title="Central Obrera Boliviana">Central Obrera Boliviana</a> (COB), became increasingly unable to effectively challenge government policy. A teachers\' strike in 1995 was defeated because the COB could not marshal the support of many of its members, including construction and factory workers.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="1997-2002_General_Banzer_Presidency">1997-2002 General Banzer Presidency</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bolivia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: 1997-2002 General Banzer Presidency">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>In the 1997 elections, General <a href="/wiki/Hugo_Banzer" title="Hugo Banzer">Hugo Banzer</a>, leader of the <a href="/wiki/Nationalist_Democratic_Action" title="Nationalist Democratic Action">Nationalist Democratic Action</a> party (ADN) and former dictator (1971&#8211;78), won 22% of the vote, while the MNR candidate won 18%. At the outset of his government, President Banzer launched a policy of using special police-units to eradicate physically the illegal coca of the Chapare region. The MIR of Jaime Paz Zamora remained a coalition-partner throughout the Banzer government, supporting this policy (called the Dignity Plan).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> The Banzer government basically continued the free-market and privatization-policies of its predecessor. The relatively robust economic growth of the mid-1990s continued until about the third year of its term in office. After that, regional, global and domestic factors contributed to a decline in economic growth. Financial crises in Argentina and Brazil, lower world prices for export commodities, and reduced employment in the coca sector depressed the Bolivian economy. The public also perceived a significant amount of public sector corruption. These factors contributed to increasing social protests during the second half of Banzer\'s term.\n</p><p>Between January 1999 and April 2000, large-scale <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2000_Cochabamba_protests" title="2000 Cochabamba protests">protests</a> erupted in <a href="/wiki/Cochabamba" title="Cochabamba">Cochabamba</a>, Bolivia\'s third largest city, in response to the <a href="/wiki/Water_privatization" title="Water privatization">privatisation of water</a> resources by foreign companies and a subsequent doubling of water prices. On 6 August 2001, Banzer resigned from office after being diagnosed with cancer. He died less than a year later. Vice President <a href="/wiki/Jorge_Quiroga" title="Jorge Quiroga">Jorge Fernando Quiroga Ram&#237;rez</a> completed the final year of his term.\n</p><p>\nIn the June 2002 national elections, former President Gonzalo S&#225;nchez de Lozada (MNR) placed first with 22.5% of the vote, followed by coca-advocate and native peasant-leader <a href="/wiki/Evo_Morales" title="Evo Morales">Evo Morales</a> (<a href="/wiki/Movement_for_Socialism_(Bolivia)" title="Movement for Socialism (Bolivia)">Movement Toward Socialism</a>, MAS) with 20.9%. </p><div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Evo_Morales_in_Ecuador_(cropped).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1688" data-file-width="1490" decoding="async" height="249" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Evo_Morales_in_Ecuador_%28cropped%29.jpg/220px-Evo_Morales_in_Ecuador_%28cropped%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Evo_Morales_in_Ecuador_%28cropped%29.jpg/330px-Evo_Morales_in_Ecuador_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Evo_Morales_in_Ecuador_%28cropped%29.jpg/440px-Evo_Morales_in_Ecuador_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Evo_Morales_in_Ecuador_(cropped).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Current President, <a href="/wiki/Evo_Morales" title="Evo Morales">Evo Morales</a></div></div></div><p> A July agreement between the MNR and the fourth-place MIR, which had again been led in the election by former President Jaime Paz Zamora, virtually ensured the election of S&#225;nchez de Lozada in the congressional run-off, and on 6 August he was sworn in for the second time. The MNR platform featured three overarching objectives: economic reactivation (and job creation), anti-<a href="/wiki/Political_corruption" title="Political corruption">corruption</a>, and social inclusion.\n</p><p>In 2003 the <a href="/wiki/Bolivian_gas_conflict" title="Bolivian gas conflict">Bolivian gas conflict</a> broke out. On 12 October 2003 the government imposed martial law in El Alto after 16 people were shot by the police and several dozen wounded in violent clashes. Faced with the option of resigning or more bloodshed, Sanchez de Lozada offered his resignation in a letter to an emergency session of Congress. After his resignation was accepted and his vice president, <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Mesa" title="Carlos Mesa">Carlos Mesa</a>, invested, he left on a commercially scheduled flight for the United States.\n</p><p>The country\'s internal situation became unfavorable for such political action on the international stage. After a resurgence of gas protests in 2005, Carlos Mesa attempted to resign in January 2005, but his offer was refused by Congress. On 22 March 2005, after weeks of new street protests from organizations accusing Mesa of bowing to U.S. corporate interests, Mesa again offered his resignation to Congress, which was accepted on 10 June. The chief justice of the Supreme Court, <a href="/wiki/Eduardo_Rodr%C3%ADguez" title="Eduardo Rodr&#237;guez">Eduardo Rodr&#237;guez</a>, was sworn as interim president to succeed the outgoing Carlos Mesa.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2005_Morales_Presidency_and_re-nationalization_of_petroleum_assets">2005 Morales Presidency and re-nationalization of petroleum assets</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bolivia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: 2005 Morales Presidency and re-nationalization of petroleum assets">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Evomorales_20050122_posesion01.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1654" data-file-width="2480" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Evomorales_20050122_posesion01.jpg/220px-Evomorales_20050122_posesion01.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Evomorales_20050122_posesion01.jpg/330px-Evomorales_20050122_posesion01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Evomorales_20050122_posesion01.jpg/440px-Evomorales_20050122_posesion01.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Evomorales_20050122_posesion01.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Evo Morales\' inauguration as President</div></div></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Evo_Morales" title="Evo Morales">Evo Morales</a> won the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bolivian_presidential_election,_2005" title="Bolivian presidential election, 2005">2005 presidential election</a> with 53.7% of the votes, an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Absolute_majority" title="Absolute majority">absolute majority</a>, unusual in Bolivian elections. On 1 May 2006, Morales caused controversy when he announced his intent to <a href="/wiki/Bolivian_gas_conflict" title="Bolivian gas conflict">re-nationalize Bolivian hydrocarbon assets</a>. Fulfilling a campaign promise, on 6 August 2006, Morales opened the <a href="/wiki/Bolivian_Constituent_Assembly" title="Bolivian Constituent Assembly">Bolivian Constituent Assembly</a> to begin writing a new constitution aimed at giving more power to the indigenous majority.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In August 2007, more conflicts arose in Sucre, as the city demanded the discussion of the seat of government inside the assembly, hoping the executive and legislative branches could return to the city, but the assembly and the government said this demand was overwhelmingly impractical and politically undesirable. In May 2008, Evo Morales was a signatory to the <a href="/wiki/UNASUR_Constitutive_Treaty" title="UNASUR Constitutive Treaty">UNASUR Constitutive Treaty</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Union_of_South_American_Nations" title="Union of South American Nations">Union of South American Nations</a>. In the 2009 national general elections, Evo Morales was re-elected with 64.22% of the vote. His party, <a href="/wiki/Movement_for_Socialism_(Bolivia)" title="Movement for Socialism (Bolivia)">Movement for Socialism</a>, also won a two-thirds majority in both houses of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_Congress_of_Bolivia" title="National Congress of Bolivia">National Congress</a>.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bolivia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Bolivia" title="Geography of Bolivia">Geography of Bolivia</a></div>\n<table class="box-Refimprove_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg"><img alt="" data-file-height="399" data-file-width="512" decoding="async" height="39" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" width="50"/></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Bolivia&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>.
