title="Cochabamba">Cochabamba</a>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>6</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Santa_Cruz_Department_(Bolivia)" title="Santa Cruz Department (Bolivia)">Santa Cruz</a></td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Santa_Cruz_de_la_Sierra" title="Santa Cruz de la Sierra">Santa Cruz de la Sierra</a>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>7</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Potos%C3%AD_Department" title="Potos&#237; Department">Potos&#237;</a></td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Potos%C3%AD" title="Potos&#237;">Potos&#237;</a>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>8</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Chuquisaca_Department" title="Chuquisaca Department">Chuquisaca</a></td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Sucre" title="Sucre">Sucre</a>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>9</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Tarija_Department" title="Tarija Department">Tarija</a></td>\n<td><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tarija,_Bolivia" title="Tarija, Bolivia">Tarija</a>\n</td>\n<td>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bolivia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Bolivia" title="Economy of Bolivia">Economy of Bolivia</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tree_map_export_2009_Bolivia.jpeg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="864" data-file-width="1106" decoding="async" height="172" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Tree_map_export_2009_Bolivia.jpeg/220px-Tree_map_export_2009_Bolivia.jpeg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Tree_map_export_2009_Bolivia.jpeg/330px-Tree_map_export_2009_Bolivia.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Tree_map_export_2009_Bolivia.jpeg/440px-Tree_map_export_2009_Bolivia.jpeg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Tree_map_export_2009_Bolivia.jpeg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Graphical depiction of Bolivia\'s product exports in 28 color-coded categories</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Edificios_de_la_paz_en_Cotahuma.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="671" data-file-width="580" decoding="async" height="255" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Edificios_de_la_paz_en_Cotahuma.png/220px-Edificios_de_la_paz_en_Cotahuma.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Edificios_de_la_paz_en_Cotahuma.png/330px-Edificios_de_la_paz_en_Cotahuma.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Edificios_de_la_paz_en_Cotahuma.png/440px-Edificios_de_la_paz_en_Cotahuma.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Edificios_de_la_paz_en_Cotahuma.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>La Paz, Bolivia</div></div></div>\n<p>Bolivia\'s estimated 2012 gross domestic product (GDP) totaled $27.43 billion at official exchange rate and $56.14 billion at purchasing power parity. Despite a series of mostly political setbacks, between 2006 and 2009 the Morales administration has spurred growth higher than at any point in the preceding 30 years. The growth was accompanied by a moderate decrease in inequality.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> A surplus budget of 1.7% (GDP) was obtained by 2012, the government runs surpluses since Morales administration reflecting a prudent economic management.\n</p><p>A major blow to the Bolivian economy came with a drastic fall in the price of tin during the early 1980s, which impacted one of Bolivia\'s main sources of income and one of its major mining industries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup> Since 1985, the government of Bolivia has implemented a far-reaching program of macroeconomic stabilization and structural reform aimed at maintaining price stability, creating conditions for sustained growth, and alleviating scarcity. A major reform of the customs service has significantly improved transparency in this area. Parallel legislative reforms have locked into place market-liberal policies, especially in the hydrocarbon and telecommunication sectors, that have encouraged private investment. Foreign investors are accorded national treatment.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Miners_at_Work_Potosi_(pixinn.net).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="681" data-file-width="1024" decoding="async" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Miners_at_Work_Potosi_%28pixinn.net%29.jpg/220px-Miners_at_Work_Potosi_%28pixinn.net%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Miners_at_Work_Potosi_%28pixinn.net%29.jpg/330px-Miners_at_Work_Potosi_%28pixinn.net%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Miners_at_Work_Potosi_%28pixinn.net%29.jpg/440px-Miners_at_Work_Potosi_%28pixinn.net%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Miners_at_Work_Potosi_(pixinn.net).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Young miners at work in <a href="/wiki/Potos%C3%AD" title="Potos&#237;">Potos&#237;</a></div></div></div>\n<p>In April 2000, Hugo Banzer, the former president of Bolivia, signed a contract with Aguas del Tunari, a private consortium, to operate and improve the water supply in Bolivia\'s third-largest city, <a href="/wiki/Cochabamba" title="Cochabamba">Cochabamba</a>. Shortly thereafter, the company tripled the water rates in that city, an action which resulted in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2000_Cochabamba_protests" title="2000 Cochabamba protests">protests and rioting</a> among those who could no longer afford clean water.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup> Amidst Bolivia\'s nationwide economic collapse and growing national unrest over the state of the economy, the Bolivian government was forced to withdraw the water contract.\n</p><p>Bolivia has the second largest <a href="/wiki/Natural_gas" title="Natural gas">natural gas</a> reserves in South America.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> The government has a long-term sales agreement to sell natural gas to Brazil through 2019. The government held a binding referendum in 2005 on the Hydrocarbon Law.\n</p><p>The US Geological Service estimates that Bolivia has 5.4 million <a href="/wiki/Cubic_ton" title="Cubic ton">cubic tonnes</a> of <a href="/wiki/Lithium" title="Lithium">lithium</a>, which represent 50%&#8211;70% of world reserves. However, to mine for it would involve disturbing the country\'s salt flats (called <a href="/wiki/Salar_de_Uyuni" title="Salar de Uyuni">Salar de Uyuni</a>), an important natural feature which boosts tourism in the region. The government does not want to destroy this unique natural landscape to meet the rising world demand for lithium.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> On the other hand, sustainable extraction of lithium is attempted by the government. This project is carried out by the public company "Recursos Evapor&#237;ticos" subsidiary of COMIBOL.\n</p><p>Once Bolivia\'s government depended heavily on foreign assistance to finance development projects and to pay the public staff. At the end of 2002, the government owed $4.5 billion to its foreign <a href="/wiki/Creditor" title="Creditor">creditors</a>, with $1.6 billion of this amount owed to other governments and most of the balance owed to multilateral development banks. Most payments to other governments have been rescheduled on several occasions since 1987 through the <a href="/wiki/Paris_Club" title="Paris Club">Paris Club</a> mechanism. External creditors have been willing to do this because the Bolivian government has generally achieved the monetary and fiscal targets set by IMF programs since 1987, though economic crises have undercut Bolivia\'s normally good record. However, by 2013 the foreign assistance is just a fraction of the government budget thanks to tax collection mainly from the profitable exports to Brazil and Argentina of natural gas.\n</p><p>The income from tourism has become increasingly important. <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Bolivia" title="Tourism in Bolivia">Bolivia\'s tourist industry</a> has grown gradually since about 1990.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign-exchange_reserves">Foreign-exchange reserves</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bolivia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Foreign-exchange reserves">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The amount in reserve currencies and <a href="/wiki/Gold" title="Gold">gold</a> held by Bolivia\'s Central Bank advanced from 1.085 billion US dollars in 2000, under <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hugo_Banzer_Suarez" title="Hugo Banzer Suarez">Hugo Banzer Suarez</a>\'s government, to 15.282 billion US dollars in 2014 under <a href="/wiki/Evo_Morales" title="Evo Morales">Evo Morales</a>\' government.\n</p>\n<table style="margin: 1em auto; padding: 0.5e text-align:left; clear:all; font-size:90%">\n<tbody><tr>\n<td colspan="6" style="background:#black; color:white; text-align: center; background-color: #9acd32;"><b><span style="font-size: 120%;">Foreign-exchange reserves 2000&#8211;2014 (MM US$)</span></b> <b><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup></b>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>\n<div class="timeline-wrapper"><map name="timeline_3b5215a092ab9df64f3cc69cf9604c4e"></map><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/timeline/3b5215a092ab9df64f3cc69cf9604c4e.png" usemap="#timeline_3b5215a092ab9df64f3cc69cf9604c4e"/></div>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td align="center" colspan="1" style="background:#f5f5f5;">Fuente: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Banco_Central_de_Bolivia" title="Banco Central de Bolivia">Banco Central de Bolivia</a>, Gr&#225;fica elaborada por: <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia" title="Wikipedia">Wikipedia</a>.\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bolivia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Air_traffic">Air traffic</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bolivia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Air traffic">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_airlines_of_Bolivia" title="List of airlines of Bolivia">List of airlines of Bolivia</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_airports_in_Bolivia" title="List of airports in Bolivia">List of airports in Bolivia</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Aviones_de_BoA_en_Cochabamba.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2448" data-file-width="3264" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Aviones_de_BoA_en_Cochabamba.jpg/220px-Aviones_de_BoA_en_Cochabamba.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Aviones_de_BoA_en_Cochabamba.jpg/330px-Aviones_de_BoA_en_Cochabamba.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Aviones_de_BoA_en_Cochabamba.jpg/440px-Aviones_de_BoA_en_Cochabamba.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Aviones_de_BoA_en_Cochabamba.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Boliviana_de_Aviaci%C3%B3n" title="Boliviana de Aviaci&#243;n">Boliviana de Aviaci&#243;n</a> (BoA) is a state-owned company and the country\'s largest airline. Two BoA Boeing 737-300s parked at <a href="/wiki/Jorge_Wilstermann_International_Airport" title="Jorge Wilstermann International Airport">Jorge Wilstermann International Airport</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>The General Directorate of Civil Aeronautics (Direcci&#243;n General de Aeron&#225;utica Civil&#8212;DGAC) formerly part of the FAB, administers a civil aeronautics school called the National Institute of Civil Aeronautics (Instituto Nacional de Aeron&#225;utica Civil&#8212;INAC), and two commercial air transport services TAM and TAB.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/TAM_%E2%80%93_Transporte_A%C3%A9reo_Militar" title="TAM &#8211; Transporte A&#233;reo Militar">TAM &#8211; Transporte A&#233;reo Militar</a> (the Bolivian Military Airline) is an airline based in La Paz, Bolivia. It is the civilian wing of the \'Fuerza A&#233;rea Boliviana\' (the Bolivian Air Force), operating passenger services to remote towns and communities in the North and Northeast of Bolivia. TAM (a.k.a. TAM Group 71) has been a part of the FAB since 1945.\n</p><p>A similar airline serving the <a href="/wiki/Beni_Department" title="Beni Department">Beni Department</a> with small planes is <a href="/wiki/L%C3%ADnea_A%C3%A9rea_Amaszonas" title="L&#237;nea A&#233;rea Amaszonas">L&#237;nea A&#233;rea Amaszonas</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> using smaller planes than TAM.\n</p><p>Although a civil transport airline, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/TAB_%E2%80%93_Transportes_A%C3%A9reos_Bolivianos" title="TAB &#8211; Transportes A&#233;reos Bolivianos">TAB &#8211; Transportes A&#233;reos Bolivianos</a>, was created as a subsidiary company of the FAB in 1977. It is subordinate to the Air Transport Management (Gerencia de Transportes A&#233;reos) and is headed by an FAB general. TAB, a charter heavy cargo airline, links Bolivia with most countries of the <a href="/wiki/Western_Hemisphere" title="Western Hemisphere">Western Hemisphere</a>; its inventory includes a fleet of Hercules C130 aircraft. TAB is headquartered adjacent to <a href="/wiki/El_Alto_International_Airport" title="El Alto International Airport">El Alto International Airport</a>. TAB flies to Miami and <a href="/wiki/Houston" title="Houston">Houston</a>, with a stop in <a href="/wiki/Panama" title="Panama">Panama</a>.\n</p><p>The three largest, and main international airports in Bolivia are <a href="/wiki/El_Alto_International_Airport" title="El Alto International Airport">El Alto International Airport</a> in La Paz, <a href="/wiki/Viru_Viru_International_Airport" title="Viru Viru International Airport">Viru Viru International Airport</a> in Santa Cruz, and <a href="/wiki/Jorge_Wilstermann_International_Airport" title="Jorge Wilstermann International Airport">Jorge Wilstermann International Airport</a> in Cochabamba.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Railways">Railways</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bolivia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Railways">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Rail_transport_in_Bolivia" title="Rail transport in Bolivia">Rail transport in Bolivia</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:402px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Railways_in_Bolivia.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="627" data-file-width="1000" decoding="async" height="251" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Railways_in_Bolivia.png/400px-Railways_in_Bolivia.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Railways_in_Bolivia.png/600px-Railways_in_Bolivia.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Railways_in_Bolivia.png/800px-Railways_in_Bolivia.png 2x" width="400"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Railways_in_Bolivia.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Railways in Bolivia <span class="nowrap">(<a class="extiw" href="//sharemap.org/public/Railways_in_Bolivia" title="sharemap:public/Railways in Bolivia">interactive map</a>)</span> <br/><span style="color:red">&#9473;&#9473;&#9473;</span> Routes with passenger traffic <br/><span style="color:black">&#9473;&#9473;&#9473;</span> Routes in usable state <br/><span style="color:black">&#183;&#183;&#183;&#183;&#183;&#183;&#183;&#183;&#183;&#183;</span> Unusable or dismantled routes</div></div></div>\n<p>Bolivia possesses an extensive but aged rail system, all in 1000&#160;mm gauge, consisting of two disconnected networks.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Technology">Technology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bolivia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Technology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Bolivia owns a communications satellite which was <a href="/wiki/Offshore_company" title="Offshore company">offshored/outsourced</a> and launched by <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a>, named <a href="/wiki/T%C3%BApac_Katari_1" title="T&#250;pac Katari 1">T&#250;pac Katari 1</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup> In 2015, it was announced that electrical power advancements include a planned $300 million nuclear reactor developed by the <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russian</a> nuclear company <a href="/wiki/Rosatom" title="Rosatom">Rosatom</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Water_supply_and_sanitation">Water supply and sanitation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bolivia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Water supply and sanitation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Water_supply_and_sanitation_in_Bolivia" title="Water supply and sanitation in Bolivia">Water supply and sanitation in Bolivia</a></div>\n<p>Bolivias\'s drinking water and <a href="/wiki/Sanitation" title="Sanitation">sanitation</a> coverage has greatly improved since 1990 due to a considerable increase in sectoral investment. However, the country has the continent\'s lowest coverage levels and services are of low quality. Political and institutional instability have contributed to the weakening of the sector\'s institutions at the national and local levels.\n</p><p>Two concessions to foreign private companies in two of the three largest cities &#8211; <a href="/wiki/Cochabamba" title="Cochabamba">Cochabamba</a> and <a href="/wiki/La_Paz" title="La Paz">La Paz</a>/<a href="/wiki/El_Alto" title="El Alto">El Alto</a> &#8211; were prematurely ended in 2000 and 2006 respectively. The country\'s second largest city, <a href="/wiki/Santa_Cruz_de_la_Sierra" title="Santa Cruz de la Sierra">Santa Cruz de la Sierra</a>, manages its own water and sanitation system relatively successfully by way of cooperatives. The government of <a href="/wiki/Evo_Morales" title="Evo Morales">Evo Morales</a> intends to strengthen citizen participation within the sector. Increasing coverage requires a substantial increase of investment financing.\n</p><p>According to the government the main problems in the sector are low access to sanitation throughout the country; low access to water in rural areas; insufficient and ineffective investments; a low visibility of community service providers; a lack of respect of indigenous customs; "technical and institutional difficulties in the design and implementation of projects"; a lack of capacity to operate and maintain infrastructure; an institutional framework that is "not consistent with the political change in the country"; "ambiguities in the social participation schemes"; a reduction in the quantity and \nquality of water due to climate change; pollution and a lack of integrated water resources management; and the lack of policies and programs for the reuse of wastewater.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PNSB_80-0"><a href="#cite_note-PNSB-80">[80]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Only 27% of the population has access to <a href="/wiki/Improved_sanitation" title="Improved sanitation">improved sanitation</a>, 80 to 88% has access to <a href="/wiki/Improved_water_source" title="Improved water source">improved water sources</a>. Coverage in urban areas is bigger than in rural ones.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-JMP_81-0"><a href="#cite_note-JMP-81">[81]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bolivia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Bolivia" title="Demographics of Bolivia">Demographics of Bolivia</a></div>\n<table class="wikitable" style="float: right; margin-left: 10px">\n<tbody><tr>\n<th colspan="4" style="text-align:center; background:#cfb;">Population<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UN_WPP_82-0"><a href="#cite_note-UN_WPP-82">[82]</a></sup>\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<th style="background:#cfb;">Year\n</th>\n<th style="background:#cfb;">Million\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="text-align:left;">1950</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">3.1\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="text-align:left;">2000</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">8.3\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="text-align:left;">2016</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">10.9\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Centro_de_La_Paz_en_Bolivia.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1920" data-file-width="2560" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Centro_de_La_Paz_en_Bolivia.JPG/220px-Centro_de_La_Paz_en_Bolivia.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Centro_de_La_Paz_en_Bolivia.JPG/330px-Centro_de_La_Paz_en_Bolivia.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Centro_de_La_Paz_en_Bolivia.JPG/440px-Centro_de_La_Paz_en_Bolivia.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Centro_de_La_Paz_en_Bolivia.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>People in La Paz city centre</div></div></div>\n<p>According to the last two censuses carried out by the Bolivian National Statistics Institute <i>(Instituto Nacional de Estad&#237;stica</i>, INE), the population increased from 8,274,325 (from which 4,123,850 were men and 4,150,475 were women) in 2001 to 10,027,254 in 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cen2012_83-0"><a href="#cite_note-Cen2012-83">[83]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In the last fifty years the Bolivian population has tripled, reaching a population growth rate of 2.25%. The growth of the population in the inter-census periods (1950&#8211;1976 and 1976&#8211;1992) was approximately 2.05%, while between the last period, 1992&#8211;2001, it reached 2.74% annually.\n</p><p>Some 62.43% of Bolivians live in urban areas, while the remaining 37.57% in rural areas. The most part of the population (70%) is concentrated in the departments of <a href="/wiki/La_Paz_Department_(Bolivia)" title="La Paz Department (Bolivia)">La Paz</a>, <a href="/wiki/Santa_Cruz_Department_(Bolivia)" title="Santa Cruz Department (Bolivia)">Santa Cruz</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cochabamba_Department" title="Cochabamba Department">Cochabamba</a>. In the <a href="/wiki/Andes" title="Andes">Andean</a> <a href="/wiki/Altiplano" title="Altiplano">Altiplano</a> region the departments of La Paz and <a href="/wiki/Oruro_Department" title="Oruro Department">Oruro</a> hold the largest percentage of population, in the valley region the largest percentage is held by the departments of Cochabamba and <a href="/wiki/Chuquisaca_Department" title="Chuquisaca Department">Chuquisaca</a>, while in the Llanos region by Santa Cruz and <a href="/wiki/Beni_Department" title="Beni Department">Beni</a>. At national level, the population density is 8.49, with variations marked between 0.8 (<a href="/wiki/Pando_Department" title="Pando Department">Pando Department</a>) and 26.2 (Cochabamba Department).\n</p><p>The largest population center is located in the so-called "central axis" and in the Llanos region. Bolivia has a young population. According to the 2011 census, 59% of the population is between 15 and 59 years old, 39% is less than 15 years old. Almost 60% of the population is younger than 25 years of age.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Genetics">Genetics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bolivia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Genetics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>According to a genetic study done on Bolivians, average values of Native American, European and African ancestry are 86%, 12.5%, and 1.5%, in individuals from La Paz and 76.8%, 21.4%, and 1.8% in individuals from Chuquisaca; respectively.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ethnic_and_racial_classifications">Ethnic and racial classifications</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bolivia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Ethnic and racial classifications">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Macheteros.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="514" data-file-width="687" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Macheteros.JPG/220px-Macheteros.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Macheteros.JPG/330px-Macheteros.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Macheteros.JPG/440px-Macheteros.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Macheteros.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Bolivian Macheteros</div></div></div>\n<p>The vast majority of Bolivians are mestizo (with the indigenous component higher than the European one), although the government has not included cultural self-identification "mestizo" in the November 2012 census.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup>\nThere are approximately three dozen native groups totaling approximately half of the Bolivian population &#8211; the largest proportion of indigenous people in Latin America. Exact numbers vary based on the wording of the ethnicity question and the available response choices. For example, the 2001 census did not provide the racial category "mestizo" as a response choice, resulting in a much higher proportion of respondents identifying themselves as belonging to one of the available indigenous ethnicity choices. <a href="/wiki/Mestizo" title="Mestizo">Mestizos</a> are distributed throughout the entire country and make up 26% of the Bolivian population. Most people assume their <i>mestizo</i> identity while at the same time identifying themselves with one or more indigenous cultures. A 2018 estimate of racial classification put mestizo (mixed white and Amerindian) at 68%, indigenous at 20%, white at 5%, <a href="/wiki/Cholo" title="Cholo">cholo</a> at 2%, black at 1%, other at 4%, while 2% were unspecified; 44% attributed themselves to some indigenous group, predominantly the linguistic categories of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Quechuas" title="Quechuas">Quechuas</a> or <a href="/wiki/Aymara_people" title="Aymara people">Aymaras</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cia_3-2"><a href="#cite_note-cia-3">[3]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/White_people" title="White people">Whites</a> comprised about 14% of the population in 2006, and are usually concentrated in the largest cities: <a href="/wiki/La_Paz" title="La Paz">La Paz</a>, <a href="/wiki/Santa_Cruz_de_la_Sierra" title="Santa Cruz de la Sierra">Santa Cruz de la Sierra</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cochabamba" title="Cochabamba">Cochabamba</a>, but as well in some minor cities like <a href="/wiki/Tarija" title="Tarija">Tarija</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sucre" title="Sucre">Sucre</a>. The ancestry of Whites and the White ancestry of Mestizos lies within the continents of <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a> and <a href="/wiki/Middle_East" title="Middle East">Middle East</a>, most notably <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a>, <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a>, <a href="/wiki/Croatia" title="Croatia">Croatia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lebanon" title="Lebanon">Lebanon</a> and <a href="/wiki/Syria" title="Syria">Syria</a>. In the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Santa_Cruz_Department,_Bolivia" title="Santa Cruz Department, Bolivia">Santa Cruz Department</a>, there are several dozen colonies of German-speaking <a href="/wiki/Russian_Mennonite" title="Russian Mennonite">Mennonites from Russia</a> totaling around 40,000 inhabitants (as of  2012<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Bolivia&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Afro-Bolivian" title="Afro-Bolivian">Afro-Bolivians</a>, descendants of <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_slave_trade" title="Atlantic slave trade">African slaves</a> who arrived in the time of the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Empire" title="Spanish Empire">Spanish Empire</a>, inhabit the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/La_Paz_Department,_Bolivia" title="La Paz Department, Bolivia">department of La Paz</a>, and are located mainly in the provinces of <a href="/wiki/Nor_Yungas_Province" title="Nor Yungas Province">Nor Yungas</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sud_Yungas_Province" title="Sud Yungas Province">Sud Yungas</a>. Slavery was abolished in Bolivia in 1831.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup> There are also important communities of <a href="/wiki/Japanese_Bolivians" title="Japanese Bolivians">Japanese</a> (14.000<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup>) and <a href="/wiki/Lebanon" title="Lebanon">Lebanese</a> (12.900<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup>).\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_of_the_Americas" title="Indigenous peoples of the Americas">Indigenous peoples</a>, also called <i>"originarios"</i> ("native" or "original") and less frequently, <i>Amerindians</i>, could be categorized by geographic area, such as <a href="/wiki/Andes" title="Andes">Andean</a>, like the <a href="/wiki/Aymara_people" title="Aymara people">Aymaras</a> and <a href="/wiki/Quechua_people" title="Quechua people">Quechuas</a> (who formed the ancient <a href="/wiki/Inca_Empire" title="Inca Empire">Inca Empire</a>), who are concentrated in the western departments of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/La_Paz_Department,_Bolivia" title="La Paz Department, Bolivia">La Paz</a>, <a href="/wiki/Potos%C3%AD_Department" title="Potos&#237; Department">Potos&#237;</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oruro_Department" title="Oruro Department">Oruro</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cochabamba_Department" title="Cochabamba Department">Cochabamba</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chuquisaca_Department" title="Chuquisaca Department">Chuquisaca</a>. There also are ethnic populations in the east, composed of the <a href="/wiki/Chiquitano" title="Chiquitano">Chiquitano</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chan%C3%A9" title="Chan&#233;">Chan&#233;</a>, <a href="/wiki/Guaran%C3%AD_people" title="Guaran&#237; people">Guaran&#237;</a> and <a href="/wiki/Moxo" title="Moxo">Moxos</a>, among others, who inhabit the departments of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Santa_Cruz_Department,_Bolivia" title="Santa Cruz Department, Bolivia">Santa Cruz</a>, <a href="/wiki/Beni_Department" title="Beni Department">Beni</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tarija_Department" title="Tarija Department">Tarija</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pando_Department" title="Pando Department">Pando</a>.\n</p><p>There are small numbers of European citizens from <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a>, <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a>, <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">Portugal</a>, as well as from other American countries, as <a href="/wiki/Argentina" title="Argentina">Argentina</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chile" title="Chile">Chile</a>, <a href="/wiki/Colombia" title="Colombia">Colombia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">Cuba</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ecuador" title="Ecuador">Ecuador</a>, the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>, <a href="/wiki/Paraguay" title="Paraguay">Paraguay</a>, <a href="/wiki/Peru" title="Peru">Peru</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">Mexico</a> and <a href="/wiki/Venezuela" title="Venezuela">Venezuela</a>, among others. There are important <a href="/wiki/Peru" title="Peru">Peruvian</a> colonies in <a href="/wiki/La_Paz" title="La Paz">La Paz</a>, <a href="/wiki/El_Alto" title="El Alto">El Alto</a> and <a href="/wiki/Santa_Cruz_de_la_Sierra" title="Santa Cruz de la Sierra">Santa Cruz de la Sierra</a>.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Indigenous_peoples">Indigenous peoples</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bolivia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Indigenous peoples">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_of_Bolivia" title="Indigenous peoples of Bolivia">Indigenous peoples of Bolivia</a> can be divided into two categories of ethnic groups: the Andeans, who are located in the <a href="/wiki/Andes" title="Andes">Andean</a> <a href="/wiki/Altiplano" title="Altiplano">Altiplano</a> and the valley region; and the lowland groups, who inhabit the warm regions of central and eastern Bolivia, including the valleys of Cochabamba Department, the Amazon Basin areas of northern La Paz Department, and the lowland departments of Beni, Pando, Santa Cruz, and Tarija (including the <a href="/wiki/Gran_Chaco" title="Gran Chaco">Gran Chaco</a> region in the southeast of the country). Large numbers of Andean peoples have also migrated to form Quechua, Aymara, and intercultural communities in the lowlands.\n</p>\n<ul><li><b>Andean ethnicities</b>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Aymara_people" title="Aymara people">Aymara people</a>. They live on the high plateau of the departments of La Paz, Oruro and Potos&#237;, as well as some small regions near the tropical flatlands.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Quechua_people" title="Quechua people">Quechua people</a>. They mostly inhabit the valleys in <a href="/wiki/Cochabamba_Department" title="Cochabamba Department">Cochabamba</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chuquisaca_Department" title="Chuquisaca Department">Chuquisaca</a>. They also inhabit some mountain regions in <a href="/wiki/Potos%C3%AD_Department" title="Potos&#237; Department">Potos&#237;</a> and <a href="/wiki/Oruro_Department" title="Oruro Department">Oruro</a>. They divide themselves into different Quechua nations, as the Tarabucos, Ucumaris, Chalchas, Chaquies, Yralipes, Tirinas, among others.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Uru_people" title="Uru people">Uru people</a></li></ul></li>\n<li><b>Ethnicities of the Eastern Lowlands</b>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Guaran%C3%AD_people" title="Guaran&#237; people">Guaran&#237;es</a>: made up of Guarayos, Pausernas, <a href="/wiki/Sirion%C3%B3" title="Sirion&#243;">Sirion&#243;s</a>, Chiriguanos, <a href="/wiki/Wich%C3%AD" title="Wich&#237;">Wich&#237;</a>, Chulipis, Taipetes, <a href="/wiki/Toba_people" title="Toba people">Tobas</a>, and Yuquis.</li>\n<li><b>Tacanas</b>: made up of Lecos, Chimanes, Araonas, and Maropas.</li>\n<li><b>Panos</b>: made up of Chacobos, Caripunas, Sinabos, Capuibos, and Guacanaguas.</li>\n<li><b>Aruacos</b>: made up of Apolistas, Baures, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Moxo_people" title="Moxo people">Moxos</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chan%C3%A9_people" title="Chan&#233; people">Chan&#233;</a>, Movimas, Cayabayas, Carabecas, and Paiconecas (Paucanacas).</li>\n<li><b>Chapacuras</b>: made up of Itenez (More), Chapacuras, Sansinonianos, Canichanas, Itonamas, Yuracares, Guatoses, and <a href="/wiki/Chiquitano" title="Chiquitano">Chiquitanos</a>.</li>\n<li><b>Botocudos</b>: made up of Bororos and Otuquis.</li>\n<li><b>Zamucos</b>: made up of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ayoreo_people" title="Ayoreo people">Ayoreos</a>.</li></ul></li></ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Language">Language</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bolivia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Language">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Bolivia" title="Languages of Bolivia">Languages of Bolivia</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Pueblos_originarios_de_Bolivia.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2672" data-file-width="2370" decoding="async" height="248" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Pueblos_originarios_de_Bolivia.png/220px-Pueblos_originarios_de_Bolivia.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Pueblos_originarios_de_Bolivia.png/330px-Pueblos_originarios_de_Bolivia.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Pueblos_originarios_de_Bolivia.png/440px-Pueblos_originarios_de_Bolivia.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Pueblos_originarios_de_Bolivia.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Geographic distribution of the indigenous languages of Bolivia</div></div></div>\n<p>Bolivia has great linguistic diversity as a result of its <a href="/wiki/Multiculturalism" title="Multiculturalism">multiculturalism</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Bolivia" title="Constitution of Bolivia">Constitution of Bolivia</a> recognizes 36 official languages besides <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">Spanish</a>: <a href="/wiki/Aymara_language" title="Aymara language">Aymara</a>, <a href="/wiki/Araona_language" title="Araona language">Araona</a>, <a href="/wiki/Baure_language" title="Baure language">Baure</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/B%C3%A9siro_language" title="B&#233;siro language">B&#233;siro</a>, <a href="/wiki/Canichana_language" title="Canichana language">Canichana</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cavine%C3%B1o_language" title="Cavine&#241;o language">Cavine&#241;o</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cayubaba_language" title="Cayubaba language">Cayubaba</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ch%C3%A1cobo_language" title="Ch&#225;cobo language">Ch&#225;cobo</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chim%C3%A1n_language" title="Chim&#225;n language">Chim&#225;n</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ese_Ejja_language" title="Ese Ejja language">Ese Ejja</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Guaran%C3%AD_language" title="Guaran&#237; language">Guaran&#237;</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Guarasuawe_language" title="Guarasuawe language">Guarasu\'we</a>, <a href="/wiki/Guarayu_language" title="Guarayu language">Guarayu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Itonama_language" title="Itonama language">Itonama</a>, <a href="/wiki/Leco_language" title="Leco language">Leco</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Machajuyai-Kallawaya" title="Machajuyai-Kallawaya">Machajuyai-Kallawaya</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Machineri_language" title="Machineri language">Machineri</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Maropa_language" title="Maropa language">Maropa</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Moje%C3%B1o-Ignaciano" title="Moje&#241;o-Ignaciano">Moje&#241;o-Ignaciano</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Moje%C3%B1o-Trinitario" title="Moje&#241;o-Trinitario">Moje&#241;o-Trinitario</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mor%C3%A9_language_(Bolivia)" title="Mor&#233; language (Bolivia)">Mor&#233;</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Moset%C3%A9n_language" title="Moset&#233;n language">Moset&#233;n</a>, <a href="/wiki/Movima_language" title="Movima language">Movima</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pacawara_language" title="Pacawara language">Pacawara</a>, <a href="/wiki/Puquina_language" title="Puquina language">Puquina</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Quechua_language" title="Quechua language">Quechua</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sirion%C3%B3_language" title="Sirion&#243; language">Sirion&#243;</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tacana_language" title="Tacana language">Tacana</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tapiet%C3%A9_language" title="Tapiet&#233; language">Tapiet&#233;</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Toromona_language" title="Toromona language">Toromona</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Uru-Chipaya" title="Uru-Chipaya">Uru-Chipaya</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Weenhayek_language" title="Weenhayek language">Weenhayek</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yaminawa_language" title="Yaminawa language">Yaminawa</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yuki_language_(Bolivia)" title="Yuki language (Bolivia)">Yuki</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yuracar%C3%A9_language" title="Yuracar&#233; language">Yuracar&#233;</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Zamuco_language" title="Zamuco language">Zamuco</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-languages_2-1"><a href="#cite_note-languages-2">[2]</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">Spanish</a> is the most spoken official language in the country, according to the 2001 census; as it is spoken by two-thirds of the population. All legal and official documents issued by the State, including the Constitution, the main private and public institutions, the media, and commercial activities, are in Spanish.\n</p><p>The main indigenous languages are: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Quechua_language" title="Quechua language">Quechua</a> (21.2% of the population in the 2001 census), <a href="/wiki/Aymara_language" title="Aymara language">Aymara</a> (14.6%), <a href="/wiki/Guarani_language" title="Guarani language">Guarani</a> (0.6%) and others (0.4%) including the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Moxos_language" title="Moxos language">Moxos</a> in the department of Beni.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cia_3-3"><a href="#cite_note-cia-3">[3]</a></sup>\n</p><p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Plautdietsch" title="Plautdietsch">Plautdietsch</a>, a <a href="/wiki/German_dialects" title="German dialects">German dialect</a>, is spoken by about 70,000 <a href="/wiki/Mennonites_in_Bolivia" title="Mennonites in Bolivia">Mennonites</a> in <a href="/wiki/Santa_Cruz_Department_(Bolivia)" title="Santa Cruz Department (Bolivia)">Santa Cruz</a>. <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a> is spoken mainly in the areas close to <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bolivia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Bolivia" title="Religion in Bolivia">Religion in Bolivia</a></div>\n<p>Bolivia is a constitutionally <a href="/wiki/Secular_state" title="Secular state">secular state</a> that guarantees the <a href="/wiki/Freedom_of_religion" title="Freedom of religion">freedom of religion</a> and the independence of government from religion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Constitute_Assembly_of_Bolivia_2007_2_90-0"><a href="#cite_note-Constitute_Assembly_of_Bolivia_2007_2-90">[90]</a></sup>\n</p><p>According to the 2001 <a href="/wiki/Census" title="Census">census</a> conducted by the <a href="/wiki/National_Institute_of_Statistics_of_Bolivia" title="National Institute of Statistics of Bolivia">National Institute of Statistics of Bolivia</a>, 78% of the population is <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Catholicism" title="Catholicism">Roman Catholic</a>, followed by 19% <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Protestant" title="Protestant">Protestant</a>, and small number of Bolivians that are <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox_Church" title="Eastern Orthodox Church">Orthodox</a>, and 3% non-religious.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Association_of_Religion_Data_Archives" title="Association of Religion Data Archives">Association of Religion Data Archives</a> (relying on the World Christian Database) records that in 2010, 92.5% of Bolivians identified as <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christian</a> (of any denomination), 3.1% identified with indigenous religion, 2.2% identified as <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Faith" title="Bah&#225;\'&#237; Faith">Bah&#225;\'&#237;</a>, 1.9% identified as <a href="/wiki/Agnosticism" title="Agnosticism">agnostic</a>, and all other groups constituted 0.1% or less.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Much of the indigenous population adheres to different traditional beliefs marked by <a href="/wiki/Inculturation" title="Inculturation">inculturation</a> or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Syncretic" title="Syncretic">syncretisim</a> with Christianity. The cult of <a href="/wiki/Pachamama" title="Pachamama">Pachamama</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup> or "Mother Earth", is notable. The veneration of the <a href="/wiki/Virgen_de_Copacabana" title="Virgen de Copacabana">Virgin of Copacabana</a>, Virgin of Urkupi&#241;a and Virgin of Socav&#243;n, is also an important feature. There also are important <a href="/wiki/Aymara_people" title="Aymara people">Aymaran communities</a> near <a href="/wiki/Lake_Titicaca" title="Lake Titicaca">Lake Titicaca</a> that have a strong devotion to <a href="/wiki/James,_son_of_Zebedee" title="James, son of Zebedee">James the Apostle</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup> Deities worshiped in Bolivia include <a href="/wiki/Ekeko" title="Ekeko">Ekeko</a>, the Aymaran god of abundance and prosperity, whose day is celebrated every 24 January, and <a href="/wiki/Guarani_mythology" title="Guarani mythology">Tup&#225;</a>, a god of the <a href="/wiki/Guaran%C3%AD_people" title="Guaran&#237; people">Guaran&#237; people</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Largest_cities_and_towns">Largest cities and towns</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bolivia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Largest cities and towns">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Approximately 67% of Bolivians live in urban areas,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-factbook_96-0"><a href="#cite_note-factbook-96">[96]</a></sup> among the lowest proportion in South America. Nevertheless, the rate of urbanization is growing steadily, at around 2.5% annually. According to the 2012 census, there are total of 3,158,691 households in Bolivia &#8211; an increase of 887,960 from 2001.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup> In 2009, 75.4% of homes were classified as a house, hut, or Pahuichi; 3.3% were apartments; 21.1% were rental residences; and 0.1% were <a href="/wiki/Mobile_home" title="Mobile home">mobile homes</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup> Most of the country\'s largest cities are located in the highlands of the west and central regions.\n</p>\n<table style="margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; width: 100%; border: 1px solid darkgray; background: #f9f9f9">\n<tbody><tr>\n<th colspan="10" style="padding:0.3em 0.75em;"><div Bolivia">Name</a>\n</th>\n<th><a href="/wiki/Departments_of_Bolivia" title="Departments of Bolivia">Department</a>\n</th>\n<th><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_cities_in_Bolivia" title="List of cities in Bolivia"> Pop.</a>\n</th>\n<th><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_cities_in_Bolivia" title="List of cities in Bolivia">Rank</a>\n</th>\n<th><a class="mw-redirect" class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_cities_in_Bolivia" title="List of cities in Bolivia"> Pop.</a></th>\n<th>\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td rowspan="11" style="text-align: center"><a class="image" Cruz de la Sierra">Santa Cruz de la Sierra</a><br/><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:La_Ceja_perspectiva.jpg" title="El Alto"><img alt="El Alto" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="787" style="text-align:right;">55,692\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="text-align:center;background:#f0f0f0;">10</td>\n<td style="text-align:left;"><a href="/wiki/Quillacollo" style="text-align:right;">137,029</td>\n<td style="text-align:center;background:#f0f0f0;">20</td>\n<td style="text-align:left;"><a href="/wiki/Tiquipaya" title="Tiquipaya">Tiquipaya</a></td>\n<td style="text-align:left;"><a href="/wiki/Cochabamba_Department" title="Cochabamba Department">Cochabamba</a></td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">53,062\n</td></tr>\n</tbody></table>\n<p><br/>\n<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bolivia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Bolivia" title="Culture of Bolivia">Culture of Bolivia</a></div>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Bolivia" title="Music of Bolivia">Music of Bolivia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Public_holidays_in_Bolivia" title="Public holidays in Bolivia">Public holidays in Bolivia</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ni%C3%B1os_ejecutando_una_tarkeada.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="489" data-file-width="652" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Ni%C3%B1os_ejecutando_una_tarkeada.jpg/220px-Ni%C3%B1os_ejecutando_una_tarkeada.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Ni%C3%B1os_ejecutando_una_tarkeada.jpg/330px-Ni%C3%B1os_ejecutando_una_tarkeada.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Ni%C3%B1os_ejecutando_una_tarkeada.jpg/440px-Ni%C3%B1os_ejecutando_una_tarkeada.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ni%C3%B1os_ejecutando_una_tarkeada.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Bolivian children playing <a href="/wiki/Tarka_(flute)" title="Tarka (flute)">tarka</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Bolivian culture has been heavily influenced by the Quechua, the Aymara, as well as the popular cultures of Latin America as a whole.\n</p><p>The cultural development is divided into three distinct periods: precolumbian, colonial, and republican. Important <a href="/wiki/Archaeology" title="Archaeology">archaeological</a> ruins, gold and silver ornaments, stone monuments, <a href="/wiki/Ceramic" title="Ceramic">ceramics</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Weaving" title="Weaving">weavings</a> remain from several important pre-Columbian cultures. Major ruins include <a href="/wiki/Tiwanaku" title="Tiwanaku">Tiwanaku</a>, <a href="/wiki/El_Fuerte_de_Samaipata" title="El Fuerte de Samaipata">El Fuerte de Samaipata</a>, <a href="/wiki/Inkallaqta" title="Inkallaqta">Inkallaqta</a> and <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Iskanawaya&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Iskanawaya (page does not exist)">Iskanawaya</a>. The country abounds in other sites that are difficult to reach and have seen little archaeological exploration.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BackgroundNote_100-0"><a href="#cite_note-BackgroundNote-100">[100]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Diablada_oruro_fraternidad.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="244" data-file-width="350" decoding="async" height="153" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Diablada_oruro_fraternidad.jpg/220px-Diablada_oruro_fraternidad.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Diablada_oruro_fraternidad.jpg/330px-Diablada_oruro_fraternidad.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/b/ba/Diablada_oruro_fraternidad.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Diablada_oruro_fraternidad.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Diablada_of_Oruro" title="Diablada of Oruro">Diablada</a>, dance primeval, typical and main of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Carnival_of_Oruro" title="Carnival of Oruro">Carnival of Oruro</a> a <a href="/wiki/Masterpieces_of_the_Oral_and_Intangible_Heritage_of_Humanity" title="Masterpieces of the Oral and Intangible Heritage of Humanity">Masterpiece of the Oral and Intangible Heritage of Humanity</a> since 2001 in Bolivia (<i>File: Fraternidad Art&#237;stica y Cultural "La Diablada"</i>)</div></div></div>\n<p>The Spanish brought their own tradition of religious art which, in the hands of local native and mestizo builders and <a href="/wiki/Artisan" title="Artisan">artisans</a>, developed into a rich and distinctive style of architecture, painting, and sculpture known as "Mestizo Baroque". The colonial period produced not only the paintings of P&#233;rez de Holgu&#237;n, Flores, Bitti, and others but also the works of skilled but unknown stonecutters, woodcarvers, goldsmiths, and silversmiths. An important body of Native Baroque religious music of the colonial period was recovered and has been performed internationally to wide acclaim since 1994.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BackgroundNote_100-1"><a href="#cite_note-BackgroundNote-100">[100]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Bolivian artists of stature in the 20th century include <a href="/wiki/Mar%C3%ADa_Luisa_Pacheco" title="Mar&#237;a Luisa Pacheco">Mar&#237;a Luisa Pacheco</a>, <a href="/wiki/Roberto_Mamani_Mamani" title="Roberto Mamani Mamani">Roberto Mamani Mamani</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alejandro_Mario_Yllanes" title="Alejandro Mario Yllanes">Alejandro Mario Yllanes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alfredo_Da_Silva" title="Alfredo Da Silva">Alfredo Da Silva</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Marina_N%C3%BA%C3%B1ez_del_Prado" title="Marina N&#250;&#241;ez del Prado">Marina N&#250;&#241;ez del Prado</a>.\n</p><p>Bolivia has a rich <a href="/wiki/Folklore" title="Folklore">folklore</a>. Its regional <a href="/wiki/Folk_music" title="Folk music">folk music</a> is distinctive and varied. The "devil dances" at the annual carnival of Oruro are one of the great folkloric events of South America, as is the lesser known carnival at <a href="/wiki/Tarabuco" title="Tarabuco">Tarabuco</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BackgroundNote_100-2"><a href="#cite_note-BackgroundNote-100">[100]</a></sup>\nThe best known of the various festivals found in the country is the "<a href="/wiki/Carnaval_de_Oruro" title="Carnaval de Oruro">Carnaval de Oruro</a>", which was among the first 19 "Masterpieces of the Oral and Intangible Heritage of Humanity", as proclaimed by UNESCO in May 2001.\n</p><p>Entertainment includes <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">football</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="the statement provides no useful information without specific information about the sport\'s popularity (December 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bolivia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Bolivia" title="Education in Bolivia">Education in Bolivia</a></div>\n<p>In 2008, following <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a> standards, Bolivia was declared free of illiteracy, making it the fourth country in South America to attain this status.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-literacyBBC_101-0"><a href="#cite_note-literacyBBC-101">[101]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Bolivia has public and private universities. Among them: Universidad Mayor, Real y Pontificia de San Francisco Xavier de Chuquisaca USFX &#8211; Sucre, founded in 1624; <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Universidad_Mayor_de_San_Andr%C3%A9s" title="Universidad Mayor de San Andr&#233;s">Universidad Mayor de San Andr&#233;s</a> UMSA &#8211; La Paz, founded in 1830; <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Universidad_Mayor_de_San_Simon" title="Universidad Mayor de San Simon">Universidad Mayor de San Simon</a> UMSS &#8211; Cochabamba, founded in 1832; <a href="/wiki/Universidad_Aut%C3%B3noma_Gabriel_Ren%C3%A9_Moreno" title="Universidad Aut&#243;noma Gabriel Ren&#233; Moreno">Universidad Aut&#243;noma Gabriel Ren&#233; Moreno</a> UAGRM &#8211; Santa Cruz de la Sierra, founded in 1880; <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Universidad_T%C3%A9cnica_de_Oruro" title="Universidad T&#233;cnica de Oruro">Universidad T&#233;cnica de Oruro</a> UTO &#8211; Oruro, founded in 1892; and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Universidad_Aut%C3%B3noma_Tom%C3%A1s_Fr%C3%ADas" title="Universidad Aut&#243;noma Tom&#225;s Fr&#237;as">Universidad Aut&#243;noma Tom&#225;s Fr&#237;as</a> UATF &#8211; Potosi, founded in 1892.\n</p><p>In 2017, Bolivia is the first country in South America in terms of funds dedicated to public education and is the second in Latin America, after Cuba.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Health">Health</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bolivia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Health">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Health_in_Bolivia" title="Health in Bolivia">Health in Bolivia</a></div>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Refresh_Bolivia" title="Refresh Bolivia">Refresh Bolivia</a></div>\n<p>Based on 2013 <i><a href="/wiki/The_World_Factbook" title="The World Factbook">The World Factbook</a></i> estimates, Bolivia is ranked 161st in <a href="/wiki/Life_expectancy" title="Life expectancy">life expectancy</a> with a number of 68.2 years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-factbook_96-1"><a href="#cite_note-factbook-96">[96]</a></sup> Life expectancy for men is 65.4 and for women is 71.1.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-factbook_96-2"><a href="#cite_note-factbook-96">[96]</a></sup> A study by the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Development_Programme" title="United Nations Development Programme">United Nations Development Programme</a> and <a href="/wiki/UNICEF" title="UNICEF">United Nations International Emergency Children\'s Fund</a> reported over 230 babies died per day in Bolivia through lack of proper care.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup> The majority of the population has no health insurance or access to healthcare.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-who.int_104-0"><a href="#cite_note-who.int-104">[104]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Demographic_and_Health_Surveys" title="Demographic and Health Surveys">Demographic and Health Surveys</a> has completed five surveys in Bolivia since 1989 on a wide range of topics.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bolivia_Surveys_105-0"><a href="#cite_note-Bolivia_Surveys-105">[105]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Between 2006 and 2016, extreme poverty in Bolivia fell from 38.2% to 16.8%. Chronic malnutrition in children under five years of age also went down by 14% and the child mortality rate was reduced by more than 50%, according to <a href="/wiki/World_Health_Organization" title="World Health Organization">World Health Organization</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bolivia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">Football</a> (<a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">Spanish</a>: F&#250;tbol, US English: Soccer) is widespread. The national team is the <a href="/wiki/Bolivia_national_football_team" title="Bolivia national football team">Bolivia national football team</a>.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Racquetball" title="Racquetball">Racquetball</a> is the second most popular sport in Bolivia as for the results in the Odesur 2018 Games held in Cochabamba.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bolivia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div aria-label="Portals" class="noprint portal plainlist tright" role="navigation" style="margin:0.5em 0 0.5em 1em;border:solid #aaa 1px">\n<ul style="display:table;box-sizing:border-box;padding:0.1em;max-width:175px;background:#f9f9f9;font-size:85%;line-height:110%;font-style:italic;font-weight:bold">\n<li style="display:table-row"><span style="display:table-cell;padding:0.2em;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center"><img alt="flag" class="noviewer thumbborder" data-file-height="750" data-file-width="1100" decoding="async" height="22" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Flag_of_Bolivia.svg/32px-Flag_of_Bolivia.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Flag_of_Bolivia.svg/48px-Flag_of_Bolivia.svg.png 1.5x,
